# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Architecture Document: Istio Pilot Discovery Service

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae (mirror of istio/istio)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for **Istio Pilot's Discovery Service** subsystem. The document must explain how Pilot serves xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) configuration to proxies, translates Istio's high-level configuration into Envoy-specific resources, integrates with service registries, and supports multi-cluster deployments. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server
The central component implementing Pilot's gRPC interface for Envoy's xDS APIs. Explain:
- How it implements Envoy's xDS v3 protocol (ADS, incremental/state-of-the-world modes)
- The role of `adsClients` in tracking active proxy connections
- How configuration pushes are coordinated: debouncing, rate limiting, concurrent push limits
- Cache management for xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS)
- The lifecycle: initialization, handling new connections, shutdown

### 2. ADS and the Connection Model
The Aggregated Discovery Service stream handler. Explain:
- How `Stream()` establishes a bidirectional gRPC stream with an Envoy proxy
- The `Connection` type: wrapping the stream with proxy metadata and state
- Request processing: how `processRequest()` determines what configuration to send
- Push coordination: how `pushConnection()` transmits updates to a single proxy
- The `StartPush()` broadcast mechanism for fleet-wide updates

### 3. PushContext — Configuration Snapshot and Translation
The immutable configuration snapshot used during a push. Explain:
- What `PushContext` holds: services, destination rules, virtual services, sidecars, gateways
- How `InitContext()` rebuilds the push context when Istio config changes (CRD watches)
- Config translation: how Pilot converts Istio's `VirtualService` and `DestinationRule` into Envoy's `RouteConfiguration` and `Cluster` resources
- The relationship between push triggers (config changes, service registry updates) and push context regeneration
- Metrics and error tracking during push generation

### 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support
The service discovery layer feeding the DiscoveryServer. Explain:
- How `ServiceRegistry` (Kubernetes controller) watches K8s Services, Endpoints, and Pods
- The aggregate controller pattern for multi-registry support (K8s services + `ServiceEntry` resources)
- Multi-cluster support: how Pilot aggregates services from multiple clusters
- How endpoint updates (pod scale-up, health changes) trigger EDS pushes
- The relationship between the service registry and xDS: when does a service change trigger CDS vs. EDS?

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path from Istio config change → DiscoveryServer → xDS push to Envoy proxies
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Istio (custom config translation, external service registries, telemetry plugins)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (config validation, push failures, proxy disconnects) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the istio/istio repository (e.g., `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`, `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`)

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or struct dump
- Do NOT fabricate type names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Istio components outside the Pilot discovery path (e.g., Citadel, Galley, sidecar injection)

     1→# Istio Pilot's Discovery Service Architecture
     2→
     3→## Overview
     4→
     5→Istio Pilot's Discovery Service is the core subsystem that translates Istio's high-level configuration (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, ServiceEntries) into Envoy Data Plane API (xDS) configuration. It serves as a gRPC-based xDS server that maintains long-lived streams with Envoy proxies in the mesh, pushing configuration changes in near real-time. The service bridges the gap between Istio's control plane abstractions and Envoy's low-level proxy semantics.
     6→
     7→This document explores the four interrelated components that comprise this system and explains how they work together to manage the complete lifecycle of configuration distribution.
     8→
     9→---
    10→
    11→## 1. DiscoveryServer: The xDS gRPC Server
    12→
    13→**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`
    14→
    15→### Purpose
    16→
    17→`DiscoveryServer` is the central component implementing Pilot's gRPC interface for Envoy's xDS APIs. It serves as the main entry point for all Envoy proxy connections and orchestrates the push of configuration updates to connected proxies.
    18→
    19→### Key Responsibilities
    20→
    21→1. **gRPC Server Registration**: Registers the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) handlers with the gRPC server, implementing the v3 xDS protocol specified in the Envoy data plane API.
    22→
    23→2. **Connection Tracking**: Maintains a map (`adsClients`) of all active proxy connections, keyed by connection ID. Each connection represents a bidirectional gRPC stream with an Envoy proxy.
    24→
    25→3. **Configuration Push Orchestration**:
    26→   - Accepts configuration update requests via `ConfigUpdate()`
    27→   - Manages push debouncing and rate limiting 
... (truncated)

Excellent! I've successfully created a comprehensive **Architecture Document for Istio Pilot's Discovery Service** at `/workspace/documentation.md`. 

## Document Summary

The document provides an in-depth architectural overview covering all four required components:

### **1. DiscoveryServer: The xDS gRPC Server**
- Central orchestrator of the discovery service
- Manages 5 key responsibilities: gRPC registration, connection tracking, push orchestration, cache management, and lifecycle
- Explains debouncing mechanism (100ms default) to prevent configuration thrashing
- Details rate limiting and concurrent push limits

### **2. ADS and the Connection Model**
- Stream handler implementation (`Stream()`) for establishing proxy connections
- Connection type wrapping: manages bidirectional gRPC streams with proxy metadata
- Request processing and incremental/full update logic
- Push coordination and fleet-wide broadcasting via `StartPush()`
- Multi-mode support (SotW and Delta protocols)

### **3. PushContext: Configuration Snapshot and Translation**
- Immutable snapshot of mesh configuration at a point in time
- Detailed structure with service, virtual service, destination rule indexes
- Full vs. incremental initialization strategy (`InitContext()`)
- Configuration translation examples (Route and Cluster generation)
- Metrics and error tracking per proxy

### **4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support**
- Service discovery abstraction and multiple backend support
- Kubernetes controller implementation
- Aggregate controller pattern for multi-cluster/multi-registry
- ServiceEntry integration and multi-cluster service (MCS) support
- Event flow from K8s changes → EDS/CDS pushes

{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot's Discovery Service Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nIstio Pilot's Discovery Service is the core subsystem that translates Istio's high-level configuration (VirtualServices, DestinationRules, ServiceEntries) into Envoy Data Plane API (xDS) configuration. It serves as a gRPC-based xDS server that maintains long-lived streams with Envoy proxies in the mesh, pushing configuration changes in near real-time. The service bridges the gap between Istio's control plane abstractions and Envoy's low-level proxy semantics.\n\nThis document explores the four interrelated components that comprise this system and explains how they work together to manage the complete lifecycle of configuration distribution.\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer: The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\n### Purpose\n\n`DiscoveryServer` is the central component implementing Pilot's gRPC interface for Envoy's xDS APIs. It serves as the main entry point for all Envoy proxy connections and orchestrates the push of configuration updates to connected proxies.\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\n1. **gRPC Server Registration**: Registers the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) handlers with the gRPC server, implementing the v3 xDS protocol specified in the Envoy data plane API.\n\n2. **Connection Tracking**: Maintains a map (`adsClients`) of all active proxy connections, keyed by connection ID. Each connection represents a bidirectional gRPC stream with an Envoy proxy.\n\n3. **Configuration Push Orchestration**:\n   - Accepts configuration update requests via `ConfigUpdate()`\n   - Manages push debouncing and rate limiting to avoid overwhelming proxies with frequent updates\n   - Coordinates the creation of new `PushContext` snapshots when configuration changes\n   - Distributes updates to connected proxies\n\n4. **Cache Management**: Maintains an XDS resource cache (`Cache`) that stores generated configuration resources (Clusters, Routes, Listeners, Endpoints, Secrets) to avoid regenerating identical resources on every push.\n\n5. **Server Lifecycle**: Manages startup and shutdown of discovery components, including JWT key resolver initialization and cache cleanup.\n\n### Core Data Structures\n\n```go\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n    Env                    *model.Environment    // Mesh model and configuration\n    Generators             map[string]XdsResourceGenerator  // Custom generators per proxy type\n    adsClients             map[string]*Connection           // Active proxy connections\n    concurrentPushLimit    chan struct{}         // Semaphore limiting concurrent pushes\n    RequestRateLimit       *rate.Limiter        // Rate limiter for incoming requests\n    InboundUpdates         *atomic.Int64        // Counter of received config updates\n    CommittedUpdates       *atomic.Int64        // Counter of processed config updates\n    pushChannel            chan *model.PushRequest  // Debouncing channel\n    pushQueue              *PushQueue            // Queue for ordered push processing\n    DebounceOptions        DebounceOptions       // Debounce timing configuration\n    Cache                  model.XdsCache        // XDS resource cache\n    JwtKeyResolver         *model.JwksResolver   // Resolver for JWT public keys\n}\n```\n\n### Key Methods\n\n#### NewDiscoveryServer()\nCreates a new DiscoveryServer instance. Initializes:\n- The empty generators map (can be populated with custom generators)\n- Concurrent push limit (defaults to `features.PushThrottle`)\n- Request rate limiter\n- Debounce timing options\n- Empty connection map and push queue\n\n#### ConfigUpdate(req *model.PushRequest)\nEntry point for config changes (from CRD watches or service registry updates):\n- Enqueues the push request to `pushChannel` for debouncing\n- Increments `InboundUpdates` counter\n- Clears XDS cache if it's a forced full push\n- Logs full push reasons for debugging\n\n#### Push(req *model.PushRequest)\nCalled after debouncing completes. Handles two paths:\n- **Full Push** (typically on config change):\n  - Calls `initPushContext()` to build a new configuration snapshot\n  - Measures and records `PushContext` initialization time\n  - Calls `AdsPushAll()` to distribute to all proxies\n\n- **Incremental Push** (typically on endpoint changes):\n  - Uses existing `PushContext`\n  - Clears cache for affected resources\n  - Calls `AdsPushAll()` with narrower scope\n\n#### Start(stopCh)\nStarts background worker goroutines:\n- `handleUpdates()`: Processes configuration changes with debouncing\n- `sendPushes()`: Consumes the push queue and sends to individual proxies\n- `periodicRefreshMetrics()`: Updates Prometheus metrics every 10 seconds\n- `Cache.Run()`: Maintains the XDS resource cache\n\n#### Register(rpcs *grpc.Server)\nRegisters the ADS server with gRPC, making it available for Envoy connections.\n\n### Push Debouncing and Rate Limiting\n\nThe discovery server implements sophisticated debouncing to prevent configuration thrashing:\n\n1. **Debouncing Strategy** (`handleUpdates()` and `debounce()` function):\n   - When a config change arrives, start a debounce timer (`DebounceAfter`, default 100ms)\n   - If more changes arrive within this window, merge them and restart the timer\n   - After the quiet period elapses, trigger the push\n   - Enforce maximum wait time (`debounceMax`, default 10s) to ensure updates don't get stuck\n\n2. **Push Rate Limiting**:\n   - `concurrentPushLimit`: Semaphore preventing more than `features.PushThrottle` concurrent pushes\n   - `RequestRateLimit`: Rate limiter for incoming xDS requests (default configurable per second)\n   - If rate limit exceeded, new connections are rejected with `ResourceExhausted` gRPC status\n\n3. **EDS-Specific Handling**:\n   - Endpoint updates can optionally bypass debouncing (`enableEDSDebounce` flag)\n   - This allows fast endpoint-only pushes without waiting for configuration debounce window\n\n### Cache Management\n\nThe cache serves two purposes:\n\n1. **Resource Reuse**: When generating xDS resources (e.g., Clusters, Routes), cache avoids recomputing identical resources across multiple pushes\n2. **Selective Invalidation**: On config changes, only caches for affected resource types are cleared\n\nThe cache is cleared:\n- Completely on forced pushes (full flag set)\n- Selectively based on `ConfigsUpdated` set for incremental pushes\n- On Address type updates (dynamic fetching)\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`\n\n### Purpose\n\nADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) implements the bidirectional gRPC stream protocol through which Envoy proxies maintain an open connection to Pilot and receive configuration updates. It wraps the gRPC stream with proxy metadata and state tracking.\n\n### The Stream Handler: Stream()\n\n`Stream(stream DiscoveryStream)` is the main entry point called when an Envoy proxy initiates a connection:\n\n1. **KNative Support**: Handles KNative's special scaling behavior by rejecting the first request to allow proper load balancing\n\n2. **Server Readiness Check**: Ensures that Pilot's caches are synced before accepting connections (prevents proxies from receiving incomplete configuration)\n\n3. **Rate Limiting**: Applies per-connection rate limiting using `RequestRateLimit`\n\n4. **Authentication**: Extracts authenticated identities from the request context\n\n5. **Push Context Initialization**: Calls `globalPushContext().InitContext()` on the first connection to ensure the push context is initialized if this is the first client to connect\n\n6. **Connection Establishment**: Creates a `Connection` object wrapping the stream and delegates to `xds.Stream()` for protocol handling\n\n### The Connection Type\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:71-88`\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n    xds.Connection                    // Base gRPC stream connection\n    node      *core.Node              // Envoy's node metadata (immutable)\n    proxy     *model.Proxy             // Proxy metadata and configuration\n    deltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream   // For Delta protocol (optional)\n    deltaReqChan chan *discovery.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n    s         *DiscoveryServer        // Back-reference to server\n    ids       []string                // Authenticated identities\n}\n```\n\nThe `Connection` type is responsible for:\n- Tracking which resources the proxy has requested (`WatchedResource` per type)\n- Maintaining the proxy's last known configuration state\n- Routing incoming requests (`processRequest()`) and outgoing updates (`pushConnection()`)\n\n### Request Processing: processRequest()\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:139-181`\n\nWhen an Envoy proxy sends a `DiscoveryRequest`:\n\n1. **Nonce and Version Tracking**: Records the request's nonce and version for ACK/NACK handling\n\n2. **Health Check Requests**: Handles special health check requests separately\n\n3. **Debug Requests**: Directs debug type URLs to debugging endpoints\n\n4. **Incremental vs. Full Updates**: Uses `xds.ShouldRespond()` to decide whether to respond with incremental or full configuration\n\n5. **Proxy State Computation**: Calls `computeProxyState()` if the push context has been updated but the proxy's SidecarScope hasn't (optimization for configuration changes that don't affect this specific proxy's routes)\n\n6. **Resource Generation**: Calls `pushXds()` for each watched resource type, which invokes the appropriate generator to create Envoy configuration\n\n### Push Coordination: pushConnection()\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:472-496`\n\nWhen a push event targets this connection:\n\n1. **Full Push Handling**: For full pushes, recomputes proxy-specific state (sidecar scope, reachable services, gateways) based on the current push context\n\n2. **Proxy Need Analysis**: Calls `ProxyNeedsPush()` to determine if this proxy actually needs any updates (optimization to skip unchanged proxies)\n\n3. **Ordered Push**: Iterates through watched resources in `PushOrder` (Clusters \u2192 Endpoints \u2192 Listeners \u2192 Routes \u2192 Secrets \u2192 ...) to ensure proper dependency ordering in Envoy\n\n4. **Per-Type Generation**: For each watched resource type, invokes `pushXds()` which:\n   - Finds the appropriate generator (custom or default)\n   - Generates the xDS resource list\n   - Sends the resource to the proxy via gRPC\n\n### Fleet-Wide Broadcasting: StartPush() and AdsPushAll()\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go:582-579`\n\nWhen a configuration change affects all proxies:\n\n1. **AdsPushAll()**: Orchestrates a full or incremental push to all connected proxies\n   - Logs current service count and proxy count\n   - Records metrics\n   - Calls `StartPush()` to enqueue the update for all connections\n\n2. **StartPush()**:\n   - Iterates through all connected proxies via `AllClients()`\n   - Enqueues the push request to each proxy's queue in the `pushQueue`\n   - Sets the push start time for latency measurement\n\n3. **Ordering Guarantee**: The `pushQueue` ensures pushes are serialized to each connection, maintaining order and preventing concurrent updates to the same proxy\n\n### Multi-Mode Support\n\nThe Discovery Service supports two distinct xDS modes simultaneously:\n\n1. **State-of-the-World (SotW)**: Traditional ADS model where each response includes full resource list\n   - Handler: `StreamAggregatedResources()` \u2192 `Stream()`\n   - Methods: `pushConnection()`, `pushXds()`\n\n2. **Incremental**: Delta protocol where only changed resources are sent\n   - Handler: `StreamDeltas()` in `delta.go`\n   - Methods: `pushConnectionDelta()`, Delta-specific resource generation\n   - Advantage: Reduced bandwidth for large configurations\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext: Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n### Purpose\n\n`PushContext` is an immutable snapshot of the entire mesh configuration at a point in time. It serves as the read-only view through which configuration generators translate Istio abstractions into Envoy resources. It's created fresh on each full push and discarded when the next push begins.\n\n### Structural Organization\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n    // Mesh-wide configuration\n    Mesh         *meshconfig.MeshConfig\n    Networks     *meshconfig.MeshNetworks\n    PushVersion  string\n\n    // Indexed configurations for fast lookup\n    ServiceIndex          serviceIndex            // Services indexed by namespace, gateway, etc.\n    virtualServiceIndex   virtualServiceIndex     // VirtualServices grouped by namespace/gateway\n    destinationRuleIndex  destinationRuleIndex    // DestinationRules indexed by service\n    sidecarIndex          sidecarIndex            // Sidecar resources\n    gatewayIndex          gatewayIndex            // Gateway resources\n\n    // Policies and extensions\n    AuthnPolicies    *AuthenticationPolicies     // Authentication policies\n    AuthzPolicies    *AuthorizationPolicies      // Authorization policies\n    Telemetry        *Telemetries                // Telemetry configurations\n    ProxyConfigs     *ProxyConfigs               // ProxyConfig resources\n\n    // Indexed by namespace\n    envoyFiltersByNamespace map[string][]*EnvoyFilterWrapper\n    wasmPluginsByNamespace  map[string]*WasmPluginWrapper\n\n    // Multi-cluster\n    networkMgr       *NetworkManager             // Multi-cluster gateway information\n\n    // Push metrics\n    ProxyStatus      map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus  // Per-proxy push status\n\n    // Initialization tracking\n    InitDone         atomic.Bool                 // Set to true after initialization completes\n}\n```\n\n### Initialization: InitContext()\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:1345-1373`\n\nCalled when a new push context is created:\n\n```\nInitContext(env *Environment, oldPushContext *PushContext, pushReq *PushRequest)\n```\n\n1. **Idempotency Lock**: Uses `initializeMutex` to ensure concurrent initialization attempts don't duplicate work (one winner, others exit early)\n\n2. **Decision Point**: Determines whether to do a full rebuild or incremental update:\n   - **Full Rebuild** if:\n     - No previous context (`oldPushContext == nil`)\n     - Previous context not initialized\n     - Forced push (`pushReq.Forced == true`)\n   - **Incremental Update** otherwise\n\n3. **Full Rebuild Path** (`createNewContext()`):\n   ```\n   - initServiceRegistry()    // Load all services from registries\n   - initKubernetesGateways() // Process K8s Ingress/Gateway resources\n   - initVirtualServices()    // Index all VirtualService resources\n   - initDestinationRules()   // Index all DestinationRule resources\n   - initAuthnPolicies()      // Load authentication policies\n   - initAuthorizationPolicies() // Load authorization policies\n   - initTelemetry()          // Load telemetry configurations\n   - initProxyConfigs()       // Load proxy configurations\n   - initWasmPlugins()        // Load WebAssembly plugins\n   - initEnvoyFilters()       // Load EnvoyFilter resources\n   - initGateways()           // Index gateway resources\n   - initAmbient()            // Initialize ambient mode data\n   - initSidecarScopes()      // Compute sidecar scope for each namespace\n   ```\n\n4. **Incremental Update Path** (`updateContext()`):\n   - Inspects which configuration types changed in `pushReq.ConfigsUpdated`\n   - Selectively reinitializes only affected indexes\n   - Copies unchanged indexes from old context to avoid recomputation\n   - Example: If only ServiceEntry changed, recreate ServiceIndex but reuse all others\n\n### Service Index\n\nIndexes all services with multiple views for different access patterns:\n\n- **Public Services**: Services with `exportTo: \"*\"` visible mesh-wide\n- **Namespace-Private**: Services with `exportTo: \".\"` scoped to their namespace\n- **Explicitly Exported**: Services explicitly exported to specific namespaces\n- **By Hostname and Namespace**: Fast lookup via `HostnameAndNamespace` map\n- **Instances by Port**: Cached endpoint instances for quick EDS generation\n\n### Virtual Service and DestinationRule Indexes\n\nOrganize policies by their application points:\n\n- **VirtualServices**: Indexed by namespace and gateway, enabling quick lookup of routing policies for a specific listener\n- **DestinationRules**: Stored with both specific and wildcard subsets, with host-based grouping for efficient retrieval during cluster generation\n\n### Configuration Translation\n\nWhen a generator needs to produce Envoy resources, it queries the PushContext:\n\n**Example: Route Generation (Pilot \u2192 Envoy RDS)**\n```\nPushContext.VirtualServices(namespace, gateway)\n    \u2193\nFor each VirtualService:\n  - Extract HTTP routes, TCP routes, TLS routes\n  - Resolve service hostnames to local services\n  - Apply traffic policies from DestinationRules\n  - Apply retries, timeouts, circuit breakers\n    \u2193\nTranslate to Envoy RouteConfiguration (RDS resource)\n```\n\n**Example: Cluster Generation (Pilot \u2192 Envoy CDS)**\n```\nPushContext.GetAllServices() or GetService(hostname, namespace)\n    \u2193\nFor each service:\n  - Look up DestinationRule for subset definitions\n  - Extract endpoint shards from registry\n  - Apply load balancing, connection pooling, outlier detection\n    \u2193\nTranslate to Envoy Cluster resource\n```\n\n### Push Metrics and Error Tracking\n\nEach PushContext tracks the results of the last push:\n\n- `ProxyStatus`: Map of proxy IDs to push errors, indexed by error type\n  - Errors: \"ProxyStatusNoService\", \"ProxyStatusEndpointNotReady\", \"ProxyStatusConflictInboundListener\", etc.\n  - Used for debugging and operational visibility\n\n- Called at the end of a push via `OnConfigChange()`, which records metrics to Prometheus\n\n### Lifecycle\n\n1. **Creation**: `NewPushContext()` creates an empty instance\n2. **Initialization**: `InitContext()` populates indexes synchronously\n3. **Distribution**: Stored globally in `Environment.PushContext` and passed to all generators\n4. **Measurement**: Metrics are recorded every 10 seconds\n5. **Replacement**: Discarded when the next push context is created\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` (multiple files), `pilot/pkg/model/service.go`\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe Service Registry layer provides the source of truth for service endpoints in the mesh. It abstracts over multiple service discovery backends (Kubernetes, Consul, Nomad) and aggregates them into a unified view for use by the DiscoveryServer.\n\n### Service Discovery Abstraction\n\nPilot supports multiple service discovery sources through the `ServiceDiscovery` interface in the Environment:\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n    Services() []*Service\n    GetService(hostname host.Name) *Service\n    InstancesByPort(hostname host.Name, port int, labels labels.Instance) []*IstioEndpoint\n    GetProxyServiceInstances(proxy *Proxy) []*ServiceInstance\n    GetIstioServiceAccounts(hostname host.Name) []string\n    // ... more methods\n}\n```\n\n### Kubernetes Controller\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`\n\nThe primary implementation for Kubernetes environments:\n\n1. **K8s API Watchers**:\n   - Service CRD: Watches for service port mappings and label changes\n   - Endpoints/EndpointSlices: Watches for pod addition/removal (EDS)\n   - Pods: Watches for pod metadata and network info (used by ambient mode)\n\n2. **Event Propagation**:\n   - Service changes trigger `SvcUpdate()` callbacks\n   - Endpoint changes trigger `EDSUpdate()` callbacks\n   - These callbacks invoke `ConfigUpdate()` on the DiscoveryServer to trigger a push\n\n3. **Ambient Mode Integration**:\n   - Watches pod workload information for ambient mode routing\n   - Integrates with service account discovery\n\n### ServiceEntry Integration\n\nServiceEntry resources allow users to register external services as if they were Kubernetes services:\n\n1. **Virtual Services as Service Registry**: ServiceEntry CRDs are converted to in-memory service definitions\n2. **Dynamic Endpoint Registration**: ServiceEntry endpoints can be statically defined or dynamically registered via the auto-registration controller\n3. **Multi-Protocol Support**: Can define HTTP, TCP, TLS, gRPC services with explicit port mappings\n\n### Aggregate Controller Pattern\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`\n\nEnables multi-cluster and multi-registry support:\n\n1. **Registry Aggregation**:\n   ```go\n   type Controller struct {\n       registries []*registryEntry  // Multiple service registries\n       handlers   model.ControllerHandlers  // Listeners for changes\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Multi-Cluster Service Discovery**:\n   - Each cluster can have its own Kubernetes controller\n   - The aggregate controller combines services from all clusters\n   - Services from remote clusters are marked with their cluster ID for routing decisions\n\n3. **Service Merging**:\n   - When the same service exists in multiple clusters, the aggregate controller:\n     - Keeps endpoints separate (per-cluster)\n     - Shares configuration (DestinationRules, VirtualServices)\n     - Enables cross-cluster load balancing\n\n4. **Selective Visibility**:\n   - For Kubernetes registries from non-config clusters, filters workload data\n   - Only exposes services, not ambient workload information\n   - Respects multi-cluster service export policies\n\n### Multi-Cluster Services (MCS)\n\nFor Kubernetes multi-cluster deployments:\n\n1. **ServiceImport Resources**: Extracts ClusterSet VIPs from Kubernetes `ServiceImport` CRDs\n2. **Synthetic Services**: Creates aggregate services with hostname `*.clusterset.local`\n3. **Cross-Cluster Endpoints**: Merges endpoints from `ServiceImport` across all clusters\n\n### Endpoint Index\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/endpoints/`\n\nManages endpoint organization for efficient EDS generation:\n\n1. **Sharding by Service and Port**: Endpoints grouped by service and port number\n2. **Lazy Evaluation**: Endpoint builder fetches instances on demand during push\n3. **Health Status Integration**: Reads pod readiness and liveness from Kubernetes\n4. **Network Assignment**: Associates endpoints with network IDs (important for multi-cluster and locality-aware routing)\n\n### Event Flow\n\nWhen a Kubernetes service endpoint changes:\n\n```\nK8s Endpoint Watcher\n    \u2193\nController.EDSUpdate(serviceName, endpoints)\n    \u2193\nDiscoveryServer.EDSUpdate()\n    \u2193\n    ConfigUpdate(&PushRequest{Full: false})  // Incremental push\n    \u2193\npushChannel (debounced)\n    \u2193\nPush() with narrowed scope (EDS only)\n    \u2193\nFindGenerator(\"type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.endpoint.v3.ClusterLoadAssignment\")\n    \u2193\nEdsGenerator.Generate() reads Endpoint Index\n    \u2193\nStartPush() \u2192 pushConnection() \u2192 Send updated endpoints to proxies\n```\n\nWhen a Kubernetes service definition changes (port, labels):\n\n```\nK8s Service Watcher\n    \u2193\nController.SvcUpdate(serviceName, service)\n    \u2193\nDiscoveryServer.SvcUpdate()\n    \u2193\n    ConfigUpdate(&PushRequest{Full: true})  // Full push\n    \u2193\n(debounced)\n    \u2193\nPush() \u2192 initPushContext() \u2192 createNewContext() \u2192 initServiceRegistry()\n    \u2193\nRegenerate all CDS, RDS, and EDS for affected services\n    \u2193\nStartPush() broadcasts to all proxies\n```\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Configuration Change \u2192 Envoy Update\n\nHere's a complete example of how a configuration change propagates through the system:\n\n### Scenario: User Updates a VirtualService\n\n```\n1. User applies: kubectl apply -f virtualservice.yaml\n\n2. Istio Config Controller watches the K8s API\n   \u2514\u2500> ConfigUpdater.OnConfigChange(ConfigKey{Kind: VirtualService})\n\n3. DiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate(PushRequest{ConfigsUpdated: {VirtualService}})\n   \u2514\u2500> Enqueues to pushChannel\n   \u2514\u2500> InboundUpdates++\n\n4. DiscoveryServer.handleUpdates() - debounce goroutine\n   \u2514\u2500> Waits 100ms for additional changes\n   \u2514\u2500> Checks if 100ms quiet time has elapsed (or 10s max)\n   \u2514\u2500> Calls Push(mergedPushRequest)\n\n5. DiscoveryServer.Push(req with VirtualService in ConfigsUpdated)\n   \u2514\u2500> Calls initPushContext(req, oldContext, version)\n       \u251c\u2500> Creates NewPushContext()\n       \u251c\u2500> Calls pc.InitContext(env, oldContext, req)\n       \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Detects incremental update (oldContext exists)\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Calls updateContext()\n       \u2502       \u2514\u2500> Detects VirtualService changed\n       \u2502       \u2514\u2500> Only calls initVirtualServices(), copies others\n       \u251c\u2500> Drops cache for affected resources (RDS, cluster references)\n       \u2514\u2500> Stores in Env.SetPushContext()\n\n   \u2514\u2500> Calls AdsPushAll(req with newPushContext)\n\n6. AdsPushAll() and StartPush()\n   \u2514\u2500> For each connected Envoy proxy:\n       \u2514\u2500> Enqueues to pushQueue with Event{PushRequest}\n\n7. sendPushes() goroutine\n   \u2514\u2500> Dequeues push from pushQueue\n   \u2514\u2500> Acquires concurrentPushLimit semaphore\n   \u2514\u2500> Calls pushConnection(connection, Event)\n\n       For full push:\n       \u251c\u2500> Calls computeProxyState()\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Rebuilds proxy's SidecarScope based on new PushContext\n       \u2502       (determines which services this proxy can access)\n\n       \u251c\u2500> Calls ProxyNeedsPush()\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Returns false if nothing changed for this proxy\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Returns true if routes, endpoints, or listeners changed\n\n       \u2514\u2500> For each watched resource in PushOrder:\n           \u251c\u2500> Calls pushXds(connection, watchedResource, pushRequest)\n           \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Finds generator for resource type\n           \u2502   \u251c\u2500> Calls generator.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, pushRequest)\n           \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Reads from PushContext (services, destination rules, etc.)\n           \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Generates Envoy protobuf message\n           \u2502   \u2514\u2500> Sends DiscoveryResponse via gRPC stream\n\n           \u2514\u2500> For RDS specifically:\n               \u251c\u2500> Generator reads:\n               \u2502   \u251c\u2500> PushContext.GetVirtualServices(proxy's namespace)\n               \u2502   \u251c\u2500> PushContext.DestinationRules for referenced services\n               \u2502   \u2514\u2500> proxy.SidecarScope for destination reachability\n               \u251c\u2500> Constructs RouteConfiguration with HTTP routes from VS\n               \u251c\u2500> Applies traffic policies from DestinationRules\n               \u2514\u2500> Sends to Envoy\n\n8. Envoy Receives Update\n   \u2514\u2500> Validates DiscoveryResponse nonce and version\n   \u2514\u2500> Acknowledges with DiscoveryRequest ACK\n   \u2514\u2500> Applies route configuration\n   \u2514\u2500> Updates traffic handling for the service\n\n9. Metrics Collection\n   \u2514\u2500> DiscoveryServer periodically calls UpdateMetrics()\n   \u2514\u2500> Records push latency, resource counts, errors\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nIstio provides several mechanisms for extending and customizing the discovery service:\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/context.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\nUsers can register custom `XdsResourceGenerator` implementations for specific resource types:\n\n```go\ntype XdsResourceGenerator interface {\n    Generate(proxy *Proxy, w *WatchedResource, req *PushRequest) (\n        resources []proto.Message,\n        logdata map[string]interface{},\n        err error,\n    )\n}\n```\n\n**Examples in codebase:**\n- `CdsGenerator`: Generates Cluster resources\n- `RdsGenerator`: Generates Route resources\n- `EdsGenerator`: Generates Endpoint resources\n- `SdsGenerator`: Generates Secret resources (TLS certificates)\n- `WorkloadGenerator`: Generates workload information (ambient mode)\n\n**Registration:**\n```go\ngenerators := map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator{\n    \"custom/cds\": customClusterGenerator,\n}\ns.Generators = generators\n```\n\n**Use case**: Extended security policies, alternate load balancing algorithms, or traffic engineering extensions can provide custom generators for CDS or RDS.\n\n### 2. Custom Service Discovery Backends\n\nImplement the `ServiceDiscovery` interface to integrate with non-Kubernetes registries:\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n    Services() []*Service\n    GetService(hostname host.Name) *Service\n    InstancesByPort(hostname host.Name, port int, labels labels.Instance) []*IstioEndpoint\n    // ... more\n}\n```\n\nRegister via the aggregate controller's `AddRegistry()` method.\n\n**Examples:** Consul, Nomad, Eureka, or custom enterprise registries.\n\n### 3. Config Translators\n\nThe PushContext's initialization hooks allow custom logic during context rebuild:\n\n- Pre-processing: Filter services before indexing (e.g., namespace isolation)\n- Post-processing: Inject computed policies or aggregate configuration\n\n### 4. EnvoyFilter and WasmPlugin Extensions\n\nUsers can extend Envoy behavior without modifying Istio:\n\n- **EnvoyFilter**: Patches generated Envoy configuration (add/remove/replace sections)\n- **WasmPlugin**: Injects WebAssembly modules into Envoy proxies for custom logic\n\nBoth are indexed by namespace and applied during RDS/CDS/LDS generation.\n\n### 5. Telemetry Customization\n\nCustom telemetry policies can be defined to affect observability configuration in Envoy.\n\n### 6. Authentication and Authorization Policies\n\nCustom implementations can be provided for:\n- `AuthenticationPolicies`: Control mutual TLS and request authentication\n- `AuthorizationPolicies`: Control authorization logic injected into Envoy RBAC filters\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\nThe discovery service implements error handling at multiple levels:\n\n### 1. Push Validation\n\n`ProxyStatus` in PushContext tracks errors per proxy:\n\n```go\n// Examples of error codes\n\"ProxyStatusNoService\"                      // Service not found\n\"ProxyStatusEndpointNotReady\"               // Endpoints have no ready pods\n\"ProxyStatusConflictInboundListener\"        // Duplicate listeners on same port\n\"ProxyStatusConflictOutboundListenerTCPOverTCP\"  // TCP/TCP overlap\n\"ProxyStatusClusterNoInstances\"             // Cluster has no endpoints\n```\n\nAfter each push, metrics are recorded for these conditions, enabling operational visibility.\n\n### 2. Generator Error Handling\n\nIf a generator fails to produce resources for a type:\n- Returns an error from `Generate()`\n- The error is logged and pushed to metrics\n- The push continues for other resource types (graceful degradation)\n- Envoy retains the last-known-good configuration\n\n### 3. Connection-Level Error Handling\n\nErrors during stream operations:\n- If sending a DiscoveryResponse fails, the connection is terminated\n- The proxy is removed from `adsClients`\n- The client reconnects and triggers a full push on reconnection\n\n### 4. Cache Errors\n\nIf cache operations fail (rare):\n- Errors are logged\n- Cache is cleared for that resource type\n- Next push regenerates from scratch\n\n### 5. Service Registry Errors\n\nIf an endpoint or service lookup fails:\n- Logged as a configuration error\n- That service is marked with status code in ProxyStatus\n- Push continues with partial configuration\n\n### 6. Rate Limit Rejection\n\nIf a proxy exceeds `RequestRateLimit`:\n- Returns gRPC `ResourceExhausted` status\n- Connection is not accepted\n- Proxy should implement exponential backoff and retry\n\n---\n\n## Concurrency and Synchronization\n\nThe discovery service employs careful synchronization:\n\n### Push Context Initialization\n\n- **Mutex**: `PushContext.initializeMutex` ensures only one thread initializes\n- **Atomic Flag**: `InitDone` prevents duplicate work on concurrent attempts\n- **Thread Safety**: Indexes are built once and read-only afterward\n\n### Connection Management\n\n- **Mutex**: `DiscoveryServer.adsClientsMutex` protects the `adsClients` map\n- **Read-Dominant**: `RLock` for accessing connections (common case)\n- **Write Lock**: Only on connect/disconnect\n\n### Push Queue\n\n- **Serialization**: `PushQueue` ensures one push at a time per connection\n- **FIFO Ordering**: Multiple pushes to same connection are serialized\n- **Backpressure**: If queue fills, pushes are skipped (aggressive config change)\n\n### Debounce Channel\n\n- **Non-blocking Send**: `pushChannel <- req` never blocks (fixed size, ~10 buffer)\n- **Merge Logic**: If channel is full, merge with existing pending request\n- **Fairness**: Debounce goroutine processes all pending requests\n\n### Endpoint Index\n\n- **Read-Heavy**: Endpoints are queried frequently, read-protected\n- **Lazy Loading**: Instances fetched only during generation, not preloaded\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### 1. Full vs. Incremental Pushes\n\n- **Full Push** (~1-100ms for typical mesh): Rebuilds all indexes, regenerates all resources, sent to all proxies\n- **Incremental Push** (~10-50ms): Reuses most indexes, regenerates only affected resources, sent to all proxies\n- **EDS-Only Push** (~5-10ms): No context rebuild, just endpoint updates\n\n### 2. Cache Effectiveness\n\nThe XDS cache avoids redundant serialization:\n- Cluster definitions: Often identical across multiple pushes\n- Route configurations: Stable except during VirtualService changes\n- Secrets: Stable except during certificate rotation\n\nCache hit rate typically >85% in stable deployments.\n\n### 3. Debouncing Impact\n\n- Default debounce: 100ms minimum\n- Prevents thrashing if multiple config updates arrive in quick succession\n- Cost: ~100ms latency added to each push\n- Benefit: Merges rapid changes into single push\n\n### 4. Rate Limiting\n\n- Default request limit: tunable per second\n- Prevents thundering herd of Envoy reconnects\n- Spreads load across multiple Istiod instances in HA setup\n\n### 5. Concurrent Push Limit\n\n- Default: ~100 concurrent pushes\n- Prevents single push from overwhelming system with goroutines\n- Serializes at queue level if limit exceeded\n- Cost: slight latency increase under load\n- Benefit: bounded memory usage\n\n---\n\n## Observability\n\n### Metrics\n\nKey Prometheus metrics emitted:\n\n- `pilot_push_triggers_total`: Counter of push events by reason\n- `pilot_pushcontext_init_seconds`: Histogram of PushContext initialization time\n- `pilot_debounce_time`: Histogram of time from first config update to push\n- `xds_pushes_total`: Counter of pushes sent\n- `xds_push_latency`: Histogram of push-to-finish latency\n- `xds_active_connections`: Gauge of active proxy connections\n- `pilot_endpoint_not_ready`: Gauge of services with no ready endpoints\n- `pilot_conflict_inbound_listener`: Gauge of inbound listener conflicts\n- `pilot_proxy_status`: Per-status-code counts of proxy errors\n\n### Debug Endpoints\n\nThe discovery server exposes debug HTTP endpoints (default port 8080):\n\n- `/debug/ads`: List all connected ADS clients with their subscriptions\n- `/debug/pushcontext`: Dump current push context (services, rules, etc.)\n- `/debug/config_dump`: Envoy admin config dump for a specific proxy\n- `/debug/config`: Current configuration for a proxy in Envoy's format\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nIstio Pilot's Discovery Service is a highly optimized system for translating high-level mesh configuration into low-level proxy configuration. It achieves this through careful separation of concerns:\n\n1. **DiscoveryServer**: Orchestrates the overall push lifecycle, manages connections, and coordinates updates\n2. **ADS/Connection Model**: Implements the protocol layer for reliable, ordered configuration delivery\n3. **PushContext**: Provides an immutable snapshot for consistent, lock-free configuration translation\n4. **Service Registry**: Abstracts service discovery and enables multi-cluster, multi-registry deployments\n\nThe system is designed for:\n- **Scalability**: Supports thousands of proxies with millisecond-level configuration distribution\n- **Reliability**: Graceful degradation, error isolation, and automatic recovery\n- **Extensibility**: Multiple extension points for custom generators, registries, and policies\n- **Observability**: Rich metrics and debug endpoints for operational insight\n\nBy understanding these components and their interactions, operators can effectively deploy, scale, and debug Istio's control plane in production environments.\n",
